Prophethood

The Prophets and Angels in the Divine Hierarchy
Author states consensus that Prophet Muhammad is best, then prophets, then angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the established order of virtue: the Prophet Muhammad is the best of creation, followed by the other prophets, then the angels.

Core Idea
After the Prophet, the prophets are the highest, then the angels.

This passage establishes a clear hierarchy of virtue among Allah's creatures. Based on consensus, the Prophet Muhammad holds the highest station. The prophets follow him, and after them come the angels. This lesson explains that order and the obligation to accept it.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the consensus on the Prophet's superiority
Read the statement that the Prophet is the best of all creatures, and that this is agreed upon. Understand that disputing this is not permissible.
2
Identify the ranking after the Prophet
The poem states: 'The prophets follow him in virtue, and after them are the angels.' Note the sequence: Prophet → prophets → angels.
3
Understand the obligation to believe
The commentary emphasizes that we must believe this ranking with certainty, as it is based on consensus and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أن أفضل المخلوقات جميعها هو نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
إذا عرفت هذا الحكم المُجمع عليه (فَمِلْ عَنِ الشَّقَاقِ) أي : المُنازعة فيه (١) ، واجزم به معتقدا صحته ؛ لأنَّه لا يجوز الإقدام على خرق الإجماع.
والأَنْبِيَا يَلُونَهُ في الفَضْلِ وَبَعْدَهُمْ مَلائِكَةُ ذِي الفَضْلِ
منه الصَّلاة والسَّلام يجب أن يُعتقد أنَّهم (يَلُونَهُ) أي:
(والأَنْبِيَاء) عليهم يتبعون نبينا محمداً ( في الفَضْل) فمرتبتهم فيه بعد مرتبته ؛ وإن تفاوتوا فيها بالنسبة للقُرب (٣) على ما يأتي في قوله: (وبعض كلّ بعضه قد يفضّل فبقيَّةُ أولى العزم (٤) مِن الرُّسل أفضلُ مِن بقيَّة الرُّسل ، ثم بقيَّة الرُّسل أفضل من الأنبياء غير الرُّسل ، والواجب اعتقاد أفضليّة الأفضل على طبق ما ورد الحكم به تفصيلا في التفصيلي ، وإجمالاً في الإجمالي، ويمتنع الهجوم على التعيين فيما لم يرد فيه توقيف ، ولهذا أَبْهِمَ النَّاظم(٥) في الفاضل
Statement that the best of all creatures is our Prophet Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. When you know this agreed-upon ruling, then turn away from dissension (i.e., dispute about it) and be certain of it, believing in its correctness, because it is not permissible to breach consensus. And the prophets follow him in virtue, and after them are the angels of virtue. From him, blessings and peace be upon him, it must be believed that they (follow him) i.e., the prophets, peace be upon them, follow our Prophet Muhammad in virtue, so their rank in it is after his rank; even if they differ in it with respect to proximity (to him), as will come in his statement: 'And some of all of them may excel others.' So the remainder of the possessors of resolve among the messengers are better than the remainder of the messengers, then the remainder of the messengers are better than the prophets other than messengers. And it is obligatory to believe in the superiority of the best according to what has come of the ruling in detail in the detailed, and in summary in the summary. And it is forbidden to rush to specify what has not been revealed. For this reason, the author left ambiguous (the superior) in the phrase 'and some of all of them may excel others.'
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a definitive statement on the ranking of prophets and angels after the Prophet Muhammad. The author begins by affirming the consensus that the Prophet is the best of all creatures, and instructs the reader to avoid dispute and firmly believe in this ruling. Then he quotes the poetic line: 'And the prophets follow him in virtue, and after them are the angels of virtue.' The commentary explains that the prophets (anbiyā) follow our Prophet in rank, though they differ among themselves in proximity to him. The author then references another line: 'And some of all of them may excel others,' and elaborates the hierarchy: the prophets of strong resolve (ulul-ʿazm) among the messengers are superior to other messengers, and other messengers are superior to prophets who are not messengers. It is obligatory to believe in this ranking as established by revelation, both in its detailed and summary forms. However, one must not rashly specify the superior in matters where no revelatory specification (tawqīf) has been given. The author (al-Laqqani) intentionally left the poem ambiguous on who is superior to whom, indicating that we affirm superiority only where revelation clearly determines it.

Key Terms
يلونه
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think angels are superior to prophets.
Correction: The passage clarifies that prophets are after the Prophet, then angels, so prophets as a group are superior to angels.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who are superior to the angels in virtue?
A) Only the Prophet Muhammad.
B) All prophets.
C) The messengers only.
D) The angels are superior.

Key Takeaway
The prophetic consensus affirms that Prophet Muhammad is the highest, followed by the other prophets, then the angels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly honor the Prophet Muhammad as the best of all creation in your daily actions, or are there moments when you prioritize others above him? What concrete step will you take today to increase your love and reverence for him?
?
If the prophets are ranked above angels, what does that reveal about the potential of humanity? How does this truth challenge the way you live your life—do you strive to rise to that potential, or do you settle for less?
?
The passage warns against disputing this hierarchy. Is there any whisper of doubt in your heart about the superiority of the Prophet? Bring it before Allah now and affirm your firm belief, and write a commitment to guard against such doubts.

The Principle of Tawqīf in Ranking among the Prophets
Author explains hierarchy among prophets and the rule of tawqif.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the internal ranking of prophets (messengers with resolve, other messengers, non-messenger prophets) and the obligation to only specify superiority based on revelation.

Core Idea
Believe in prophetic rankings as revealed, do not speculate beyond revelation.

The previous lesson established that prophets are after the Prophet. Now we delve into the hierarchy among them: the prophets of strong resolve are best, then other messengers, then prophets who are not messengers. We also learn the crucial principle that we must not assign superiority without revelation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the internal hierarchy
The poem says 'some of them excel others' and the commentary specifies: ulul-ʿazm messengers > other messengers > non-messenger prophets. Memorize this order.
2
Grasp the obligation of belief based on tawqif
The commentary states we must believe in superiority as per revelation in detail or summary. We cannot assert who is better without explicit divine specification.
3
See the author's intentional ambiguity
The poet left ambiguous who excels whom in some cases, because such details are not revealed. This teaches humility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

والأَنْبِيَا يَلُونَهُ في الفَضْلِ وَبَعْدَهُمْ مَلائِكَةُ ذِي الفَضْلِ

And it is forbidden to rush to specify what has not been revealed. For this reason, the author left ambiguous (the superior) in the phrase 'and some of all of them may excel others.'

Then he quotes the poetic line: 'And the prophets follow him in virtue, and after them are the angels of virtue.' Misconception: Some think all prophets are equal in rank or that we can rank them by personal opinion.

According to the passage, who are the highest among the prophets after the Prophet Muhammad?
A) All messengers

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself comparing the status of prophets or even people based on your own preferences? How does the principle of tawqīf challenge you to submit entirely to divine decree without adding your own opinions?
?
When you think about the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), do you believe he is the best simply because the Qur'an says so, or do you sometimes seek external justifications? This lesson demands that your conviction be anchored solely in revelation. Where does your faith truly rest?
?
If tomorrow you stood before Allah and He asked you: 'By what authority did you rank My prophets?' would your answer be based on His words or on your own speculations? Commit today to never speak about prophetic superiority except where the text speaks clearly.

Qur'anic Evidence for Prophets' Superiority to Angels
Presents transmitted evidence for prophets' superiority and mentions a minority view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the transmitted (naqli) evidence used by the Ash'ari majority to argue for the superiority of prophets over angels, and the minority view that angels are superior.

Core Idea
The command for angels to prostrate to Adam proves prophets are superior.

The Ash'ari majority relies on a clear Qur'anic command to establish the superiority of prophets over angels. This passage presents that evidence along with a minority counter-position. Understanding this debate clarifies a key point in Islamic theology regarding the rank of prophets and angels.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the meaning.
2
Identify the main evidence
Look for the Qur'anic verse cited: the command for angels to prostrate to Adam. Understand that prostration implies veneration.
3
Understand the logical implication
The passage argues that a wise being would not command a superior to serve an inferior. Thus, Adam must be superior to the angels who were commanded to prostrate.
This is the core reasoning of the majority.
4
Note the minority view and the exception
The passage mentions that al-Qadi, al-Halimi, and the Mu'tazila hold that angels are superior to prophets, except for Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).
Pay attention to the exception; it is often misunderstood.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this distinction matters for 'aqidah and how it fits into the broader discussion of prophethood and angelology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أدلة الجمهور النقلية على أفضلية الأنبياء]
هذا ما قال به جمهورُ أصحابنا الأشاعرة تمسكاً بمثل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ قُلْنَا لِلْمَلَبِكَةِ اسْجُدُوا لِآدَمَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٣٤]. أمرهم بالسجود تعظيما له ؛ فلو لم يكن آدم أفضل منهم لَمَا أُمروا بالسُّجود له ؛ لأنَّ الحكيم لا يأمرُ الأفضل بخدمة المفضول ، وذهبَ القاضي وأبو عبد الله الحليمي (۱) في آخرين كالمعتزلة إلى أنَّ الملائكة أفضل من الأنبياء (۲) ، قال القاضي تاج الدين بن الشبكي (۳) : ليس (۱) هو الإمام الحافظ أبو عبد الله الحسين بن الحسن بن محمد بن حليم الشافعي الأشعري، علامة المعقول والمنقول، وقد عُرف بالحليمي الجرجاني نسبة إلى جده حليم، ولد سنة (۳۳۸هـ) وتوفي سنة (٤٠٣ هـ). قال عنه سنة (٤٠٣ هـ). قال عنه الإمام السبكي أحد أئمة الدهر، وشيخ الشافعيين بما وراء النهر. وقال عنه ابن قاضي شهبة : كان الحليمي رجلاً عظيم القدر، لا يحيط بكنه علمه إلا غواص من كتبه المهمة التي وصلتنا : كتاب المنهاج في شعب الإيمان . (۲) قوله : ( إلى أنَّ الملائكة أفضل من الأنبياء أي: سوى نبينا ، لما تقدم أنه مستثنى من محل الخلاف في أفضلية الصنفين ، إلا ما شذ به الزمخشري . الشنواني.
(۳) الإمام العلم المُحقق: تاج الدين عبد الوهاب بن علي بن عبد الكافي السبكي الشافعي=
From the transmitted evidences of the majority on the superiority of the prophets: This is what the majority of our Ash'ari companions said, adhering to something like His saying, Exalted is He: 'And when We said to the angels, prostrate to Adam' [Al-Baqara 2:34]. He commanded them to prostrate in veneration of him; so if Adam were not better than them, they would not have been commanded to prostrate to him, because the wise does not command the superior to serve the inferior. And al-Qadi and Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi (1) among others like the Mu'tazila went to the view that angels are better than prophets (2). Al-Qadi Taj al-Din ibn al-Subki (3) said: 'Not ...' (1) He is the Imam, the Hafiz, Abu Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Halim al-Shafi'i al-Ash'ari, a scholar of the rational and transmitted sciences, known as al-Halimi al-Jurjani relative to his grandfather Halim, born in 338 AH and died in 403 AH. Al-Subki said of him: one of the imams of the age, and the shaykh of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana. Ibn Qadi Shuhba said: al-Halimi was a man of great stature; only a diver can encompass the depth of his knowledge from his important books that have reached us: the book al-Minhaj fi Shu'ab al-Iman. (2) His saying: 'that angels are better than prophets' means except our Prophet, because it has preceded that he is excluded from the locus of disagreement concerning the superiority of the two classes, except for what al-Zamakhshari diverged with. Al-Shanwani. (3) The learned, verifying Imam: Taj al-Din Abd al-Wahhab ibn Ali ibn Abd al-Kafi al-Subki al-Shafi'i =
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage presents a transmitted (naqli) proof from the Ash'ari majority that prophets are superior to angels. The evidence is the Qur'anic command for angels to prostrate to Adam; prostration is an act of veneration, and a wise being would not command a superior to venerate an inferior, thus Adam is superior. The passage then notes a minority view—attributed to al-Qadi (likely al-Baqillani?), Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi, and the Mu'tazila—that angels are superior to prophets, except for Prophet Muhammad. The footnote explains that the Prophet is excluded from this disagreement, and al-Zamakhshari held a divergent opinion. A biographical note on al-Halimi is also included.

Key Terms
أدلة نقلية
سجود
تفضيل
جمهور
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the minority view (angels superior) includes Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).
Correction: The minority view excludes Prophet Muhammad; he is considered superior to angels by consensus except for a few.

Checkpoint
What Qur'anic verse does the Ash'ari majority use to argue for the superiority of prophets over angels?
A) And when We said to the angels, prostrate to Adam (2:34)
B) And We have honored the children of Adam (17:70)
C) He taught Adam all the names (2:31)
D) He created man from clay (55:14)

Key Takeaway
The prostration command in the Qur'an is the primary transmitted evidence for the Ash'ari position that prophets are superior to angels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah commanded the angels to prostrate to Adam, do you truly feel the weight of your own human dignity as a descendant of Adam? If prophets are superior to angels, what does that demand of you in terms of gratitude and obedience?
?
The minority view that angels are superior to prophets (except Muhammad) might tempt you to feel insignificant. But what if your faith in prophethood is meant to elevate your own sense of purpose? Are you living as though your prophethood-based guidance is more valuable than any angelic inspiration?
?
If the prostration of angels is a sign of Adam's honor, then every act of humility from you—prostrating in prayer, lowering yourself before Allah—is a return to that original station. Is your prayer a mere ritual, or does it consciously reconnect you to the honor of being human?

Prophethood

Majority Proof for Prophets' Superiority Over Angels
Quranic proof for prophets' superiority and mention of opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the transmitted proof used by the Ash'ari majority to argue that prophets are superior to angels, and you will be aware of the opposing view held by some scholars.

Core Idea
The command for angels to prostrate to Adam proves his superiority over them.

In this lesson, we examine a key transmitted proof from the Quran that the Ash'ari majority uses to establish the superiority of prophets over angels. The proof hinges on the command for angels to prostrate to Adam, which implies Adam's greater rank. We will also briefly note that some scholars held the opposite view, setting the stage for further discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic text and its literal translation to grasp the author's wording and flow.
Pay attention to the key terms like 'الجمهور' and 'الأشاعرة'.
2
Understand the logical argument
Analyze the reasoning: The command to prostrate was an honor; if Adam were inferior, the Wise would not command the superior to serve the inferior. Therefore, Adam must be superior.
This is a syllogistic argument based on divine wisdom.
3
Identify the opposing view
Note that al-Qadi and Abu 'Abdullah al-Halimi, along with the Mu'tazila, held that angels are superior. Consider why they might disagree.
The next lesson continues with Ibn al-Subki's response.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أدلة الجمهور النقلية على أفضلية الأنبياء] هذا ما قال به جمهورُ أصحابنا الأشاعرة تمسكاً بمثل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ قُلْنَا لِلْمَلَبِكَةِ اسْجُدُوا لِآدَمَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٣٤]. أمرهم بالسجود تعظيما له ؛ فلو لم يكن آدم أفضل منهم لَمَا أُمروا بالسُّجود له ؛ لأنَّ الحكيم لا يأمرُ الأفضل بخدمة المفضول ، وذهبَ القاضي وأبو عبد الله الحليمي (۱) في آخرين كالمعتزلة إلى أنَّ الملائكة أفضل من الأنبياء (۲) ، قال القاضي تاج الدين بن الشبكي (۳) : ليس...
From the transmitted proofs of the majority on the superiority of prophets: This is what the majority of our Ash'ari scholars said, adhering to the like of His saying, the Most High: {And [mention] when We said to the angels, 'Prostrate to Adam'} [al-Baqarah: 34]. He commanded them to prostrate as an honor to him; so if Adam had not been better than them, they would not have been commanded to prostrate to him; because the Wise does not command the superior to serve the inferior. And al-Qadi and Abu 'Abdullah al-Halimi (1) along with others like the Mu'tazila held that angels are better than prophets (2).
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage presents a transmitted (naqli) proof used by the Ash'ari majority to establish the superiority of prophets over angels. The proof is the Quranic verse in which Allah commanded the angels to prostrate to Adam. The argument proceeds as follows: The command was an act of honoring Adam. If Adam were not superior to the angels, the Wise (al-Hakim) would not command the superior (the angel) to serve the inferior (Adam). Since the command was given, Adam must be superior. After presenting this proof, the author mentions that some scholars held the opposite view: al-Qadi (likely Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar or another) and Abu 'Abdullah al-Halimi, along with the Mu'tazila, claimed that angels are superior to prophets. The passage ends with a reference to Taju al-Din ibn al-Subki, whose statement will follow in the next lesson.

Key Terms
الجمهور
الأشاعرة
سجود الملائكة لآدم
أفضلية الأنبياء
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof is universally accepted and settles the issue.
Correction: The passage itself notes that a minority (including the Mu'tazila) holds the opposite view, so it is not a settled matter among all scholars.

Checkpoint
What is the main Quranic proof for the superiority of prophets over angels according to the Ash'ari majority?
A) The angels asked for forgiveness for Adam
B) The command for angels to prostrate to Adam
C) The story of Adam's creation from clay
D) The angels' confession of ignorance

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari majority uses the command for angels to prostrate to Adam as a transmitted proof for prophets' superiority, but a minority holds the opposite view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the command to prostrate to Adam shows his superiority, what does that say about the honor Allah has given to humanity? Do you truly believe in your own potential for honor through obedience, or do you act as if you are lower than you are? This week, commit to one act that reflects the dignity Allah gave you.
?
The dissenting scholars (al-Qadi, al-Halimi) held that angels are superior despite the apparent proof. How do you react when respected scholars disagree on an issue? Do you dig into your own opinion, or do you leave room for humility? Examine your heart: is your confidence in a matter of creed based on evidence or on attachment to a group?
?
Angels obeyed the command to prostrate to Adam without question. Do you obey Allah's commands to honor His prophets (by following their teachings) with the same immediacy? Think of one command from the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) that you have been neglecting. What will you do to show you honor him more than you honor your own desires?

The Ruling on Debating Prophetic Superiority over Angels
The author discusses the ruling on debating prophetic superiority over angels and cites a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling on debating the superiority of prophets over angels and the importance of relying on decisive proofs in such matters.

Core Idea
Debating theological preferences without decisive proof is dangerous; silence is safer.

This lesson examines a crucial ruling from classical Sunni theology: the permissibility and danger of debating whether prophets are superior to angels. The author cites a hadith to caution against entering such debates without a clear proof, while affirming the general belief in the Prophet's superiority over all creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation to grasp the author's argument.
Notice the careful distinctions the author makes.
2
Identify the key ruling
The author states that believing in human superiority over angels is obligatory, but if one is completely ignorant of this specific issue, they are not sinful. Understand the nuance.
This shows the author's precision in defining what is required belief.
3
Understand the caution
The author warns that entering into preference without a decisive proof is dangerous and a judgment where we are unqualified. Recognize the principle: safety in silence.
This is a key adab (etiquette) in theological disputes.
4
Analyze the hadith
Examine the hadith 'Do not prefer me over Yunus ibn Matta.' The author explains its intent is to prohibit unnecessary debate, not to negate the Prophet's superiority. Reflect on the difference.
This corrects a common misunderstanding.
5
Affirm the final teaching
The author concludes by affirming that Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation and lists the best of people after prophets and angels. Note how the author balances caution with affirmation.
This shows the author's positive stance despite the caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أدلة الجمهور النقلية على أفضلية الأنبياء
تفضيل البشر على الملك مما يجب اعتقاده ويضر الجهل به، ولو لقي الله ساذجا من المسألة بالكلية لم يكن عليه إثم، فما هي مما كلف الناس بمعرفته، والسلامة في السكوت عن هذه المسألة، والدخول في التفضيل بين هذين الصنفين الكريمين على الله تعالى من غير ورود دليل قاطع دخول في خطر عظيم، وحكم في مكان لسنا أهلا للحكم فيه، وقد ورد ما يمنع من الدخول في ذلك كقوله: لا تفضلوني على يونس بن متى إذ المراد به: لا تدخلوا في أمر لا يعنيكم، وإلا فنحن قاطعون بأنه أفضل من يونس، والذي ينشرح له الصدر ويثلج له الخاطر.. إطلاق القول بأن نبينا محمدا صلى الله عليه وسلم خير الخلق أجمعين من ملك وبشر، وخير الناس بعد الأنبياء والملائكة: أبو بكر، ثم عمر، ثم عثمان، ثم علي، رضي الله تعالى عنهم أجمعين، انتهى.
From the transmitted proofs of the majority on the superiority of the prophets: Preferring humans over angels is something that must be believed and ignorance of it is harmful, but if someone meets God with a blank mind [صالح] concerning this matter entirely, there is no sin upon him, for it is not among what people are obligated to know. Safety lies in silence concerning this matter, and entering into preference between these two noble kinds over God Almighty without a decisive proof is entering into great danger, and a judgment in a place where we are not worthy to judge. There has come what prevents entering into that, such as His saying: 'Do not prefer me over Yunus ibn Matta,' the intent of which is: Do not enter into a matter that does not concern you. Otherwise, we are certain that he (the Prophet) is better than Yunus. What expands the chest and comforts the heart is the absolute statement that our Prophet Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, is the best of all creation, from angel and human, and the best of people after the prophets and angels are: Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, may God be pleased with them all. End.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the debate about whether prophets are superior to angels. The author begins by stating that belief in human superiority over angels is obligatory and ignorance is harmful, but if someone is completely unaware of the issue, they are not sinful because it is not a required belief. Then he advises that safety lies in silence on this matter, and engaging in preference without a decisive proof is dangerous. He supports this with the hadith 'Do not prefer me over Yunus ibn Matta,' explaining that it means do not enter into a matter that does not concern you, not that the Prophet is not superior. He then affirms the general belief that Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation, and after prophets and angels, the best are the four rightly-guided caliphs in order.

Key Terms
تفضيل
دليل قاطع
لا تفضلوني على يونس بن متى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'Do not prefer me over Yunus ibn Matta' means that Prophet Muhammad is not superior to Yunus.
Correction: The hadith is meant to prohibit entering into debates about comparative merits without decisive proof, not to deny the Prophet's superiority.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say safety lies in silence regarding the preference between prophets and angels?
A) Because the matter is not obligatory to believe.
B) Because there is no decisive proof to settle it definitively.
C) Because the hadith explicitly forbids any discussion.
D) Because angels are clearly superior.

Key Takeaway
Debating theological preferences without clear evidence is dangerous; it is sufficient to affirm the general belief in the Prophet's superiority over all creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author says safety lies in silence. Is there a theological question or comparison you have been discussing that you should instead leave alone? What is preventing you from letting it go?
?
The Prophet ﷺ warned against preferring him over Yunus to stop unnecessary debate. Where in your life do you find yourself comparing people or positions in a way that leads to harm? Can you replace that habit with simple affirmation of good without comparison?

The Preference Among Prophets and Angels: A Detailed Hierarchy
Explains tafḍīl among prophets and angels and lists the hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in the superiority of some prophets and angels over others, and the full hierarchy as taught by Sanusi.

Core Idea
Prophets and angels are ranked, with Muhammad ﷺ at the top in a divinely ordered chain.

This lesson addresses a key question: are all prophets equal? The answer is no—some are preferred over others by Allah's wisdom. Sanusi explains this using Quranic evidence and then lays out a complete hierarchy of all created beings, starting with Muhammad ﷺ as the best. This hierarchy helps us appreciate the unique status of our Prophet and the messengers before him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very organized, list-like structure in the summary.
2
Identify the Quranic proofs for tafḍīl
The passage cites two verses (17:55 and 2:253) for prophets and one verse (22:75) for angels. Underline these in the passage and note how they support the claim.
3
Trace the hierarchy step by step
From the summary, list the categories in order from top to bottom: Muhammad, Ibrahim, Musa, 'Isa, Nuh, then the rest of the messengers, then non-messenger prophets, then the heads of messenger angels, then the rest. Notice how the hierarchy continues beyond what is provided.
The text ends abruptly with 'ثُمَّ' (then), so the hierarchy continues but is not fully given.
4
Reflect on the doctrine of preference
Ask yourself: Why does this matter? It affirms that Allah chooses some over others by wisdom, and that no one should object to this divine preference.
This connects to the common misunderstanding that preference implies deficiency in those lower.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَبَعْضُ كُلُّ مِن الأنبياء والملائكة (بَعْضَهُ قَدْ يَفْضُلُ) يعني : أنَّ مِمَّا يجب اعتقاده أنَّ بعض الأنبياء كأولي العزم أفضلُ مِن غيرهم، وبعض أولي العزم كنبينا محمد الله أفضل من غيره منهم ، كإبراهيم ، وهو أفضلُ ممَّن بقي ؛ لقوله تعالى: (وَلَقَدْ فَضَّلْنَا بَعْضَ النَّبِيِّينَ عَلَى بَعْضٍ [الإسراء: ٥٥] (تِلْكَ الرُّسُلُ فَضَّلْنَا بَعْضَهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ [البقرة: ٢٥٣] وأنَّ بعض الملائكة كالرسل منهم أفضل من غيرهم منهم ، وبعض الرُّسل منهم كجبريل أفضل من غيره منهم كميكائيل، وهو أفضل ممَّن بقي ؛ لقوله تعالى: (اللَّهُ يَصْطَفِي مِنَ الْمَلَائِكَةِ رُسُلًا [الحج: ٧٥] .
وتلخيص ما أشار إليه أوَّلاً وآخرًا : أنَّ نبينا محمدًا صلى الله عليه وسلم أفضل المخلوقات على الإطلاق، ويليه إبراهيم ، ثمَّ موسى ، ثمَّ عيسى ، ثمَّ نوح، ثمَّ بقيَّة الرُّسل ، ثمَّ الأنبياء غيرُ الرُّسل ، ثمَّ هم فيما بينهم متفاضلون أيضا عند الله ، ثُمَّ رؤوس رُسل الملائكة ، ثمَّ مَن يليه منهم، ثم بقيَّة رسلهم، ثمَّ
And some of each from prophets and angels: some of them may surpass another. Meaning: That among what must be believed is that some prophets, like the ulu al-azm (the resolute ones), are better than others; and some of the ulu al-azm, like our Prophet Muhammad ﷺ, is better than the others among them, like Ibrahim, and he is better than the rest; due to His saying: 'We have preferred some prophets over others' (17:55); 'Those messengers, We preferred some of them over others' (2:253). And that some angels, like the messengers among them, are better than the others among them; and some of their messengers, like Jibril, is better than the others among them, like Mika'il, and he is better than the rest; due to His saying: 'Allah chooses messengers from the angels' (22:75). And a summary of what he pointed to firstly and lastly: That our Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is the best of all creations absolutely, followed by Ibrahim, then Musa, then 'Isa, then Nuh, then the rest of the messengers, then the non-messenger prophets, then they among themselves are also varying in excellence with Allah, then the heads of the messenger angels, then those who follow them among them, then the rest of their messengers, then...
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage first explains the line of the poem meaning that there is preference among individuals within the categories of prophets and angels. It states that it is obligatory to believe that some prophets are better than others, citing the Quran (17:55, 2:253). Specifically, among the ulu al-azm (the five major prophets), Muhammad is the best, then Ibrahim. Similarly, among angels, messengers are better, and among them Jibril is best, citing Quran 22:75. The passage then provides a comprehensive hierarchy from the best of all creation (Muhammad) down to the rest of the angel messengers, showing a detailed ranking order.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that preference implies deficiency or that all prophets are equal in rank.
Correction: Preference does not imply deficiency; it simply reflects Allah's wisdom and mercy in bestowing greater honor upon some. All prophets are truthful and chosen, but their ranks vary.

The Hierarchy of Prophets and Angels
Sanusi enumerates the hierarchy of prophets and angels with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligatory belief in the superiority of some prophets and angels over others, and the specific hierarchy affirmed by the Quran.

Core Idea
Prophets and angels are not all equal; some are superior by divine decree.

This passage from the Jawharat al-Tawhid explains a fundamental tenet of Sunni theology: that among prophets and angels, there is a divinely ordained hierarchy. The author, Sanusi, cites Quranic verses to prove that some are superior to others, particularly the ‘ulu al-‘azm (resolute prophets) and the messenger angels. He then summarizes the complete hierarchy. Let’s explore the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalyzing. Then read the English translation to get the gist. Pay attention to the logical flow.
The Arabic may feel dense; the translation clarifies the structure.
2
Identify the two groups and their subdivisions
Look for how the passage divides prophets (into resolute ones and others) and angels (into messengers and others). Notice which individuals are singled out.
3
Note the Quranic proofs
Two Quranic verses are cited for prophets and one for angels. Understand how these verses support the claim of superiority.
Verses: 17:55, 2:253, 22:75.
4
Understand the summary hierarchy
The passage ends with a detailed ranking from best to lesser. Memorize the order: Muhammad, Ibrahim, Musa, Isa, Nuh, then rest of messengers, then non-messenger prophets, then angelic hierarchy.
The hierarchy among angels is similarly tiered.
5
Reflect on theological significance
Ask yourself: Why does this belief matter? It affirms divine wisdom in ranking creation without diminishing the honor of prophethood or angelhood.

قسم النبوات ( وَبَعْضُ كُلُّ مِن الأنبياء والملائكة (بَعْضَهُ قَدْ يَفْضُلُ) يعني : أنَّ مِمَّا يجب اعتقاده أنَّ بعض الأنبياء كأولي العزم أفضلُ مِن غيرهم، وبعض أولي العزم كنبينا محمد الله أفضل من غيره منهم ، كإبراهيم ، وهو أفضلُ ممَّن بقي ؛ لقوله تعالى: (وَلَقَدْ فَضَّلْنَا بَعْضَ النَّبِكَنَ عَلَى بَعْضٍ [الإسراء: ٥٥] تِلْكَ الرُّسُلُ فَضَّلْنَا بَعْضَهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٣] وأنَّ بعض الملائكة كالرسل منهم أفضل من غيرهم منهم ، وبعض الرُّسل منهم كجبريل أفضل من غيره منهم كميكائيل، وهو أفضل ممَّن بقي ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿اللَّهُ يَصْطَفِي مِنَ الْمَلَكَةِ رُسُلًا ﴾ [الحج: ٧٥] . وتلخيص ما أشار إليه أوَّلاً وآخرًا : أنَّ نبينا محمدًا صلى الله عليه وسلم أفضل المخلوقات على الإطلاق، ويليه إبراهيم ، ثمَّ موسى ، ثمَّ عيسى ، ثمَّ نوح، ثمَّ بقيَّة الرُّسل ، ثمَّ الأنبياء غيرُ الرُّسل ، ثمَّ هم فيما بينهم متفاضلون أيضا عند الله ، ثُمَّ أَرْأَسُ رُسل الملائكة ، ثمَّ مَن يليه منهم، ثم بقيَّة رسلهم، ثمَّ
Section on Prophethood: 'And some of each from the prophets and angels, some of them are superior.' Meaning: That from what is obligatory to believe is that some prophets, like the resolute ones, are better than others, and some of the resolute ones, like our Prophet Muhammad (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) are better than others among them, such as Ibrahim, and he is better than whoever remains; due to His statement, the Exalted: 'And We have favored some prophets over others' [17:55] and 'Those messengers, We favored some of them over others' [2:253]; and that some angels, like the messengers among them, are better than others among them, and some of the messengers among them, like Jibril, are better than others among them, like Mika'il, and he is better than whoever remains; due to His statement, the Exalted: 'Allah selects from the angels messengers' [22:75]. And a summary of what he indicated firstly and lastly: That our Prophet Muhammad (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) is the best of creatures absolutely, followed by Ibrahim, then Musa, then 'Isa, then Nuh, then the rest of the messengers, then the prophets who are not messengers, then they among themselves are also distinguished in rank with Allah, then the heads of the messengers of the angels, then those who follow them among them, then the rest of their messengers, then...
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage defines and proves the obligatory belief in the hierarchy among prophets and angels. It begins by stating the general principle that some prophets and angels are superior to others. It then provides examples: among prophets, the 'ulu al-'azm (resolute ones) are best, and among them our Prophet Muhammad is the best, followed by Ibrahim. The proof is from Quranic verses. Similarly among angels, the messengers are best, and among them Jibril is best, followed by Mika'il. The passage then summarizes the full hierarchy: Muhammad is the best of all creation, then Ibrahim, Musa, 'Isa, Nuh, then the rest of the messengers, then the non-messenger prophets, then within each group they are further distinguished. Then the hierarchy of angels: the heads of the angelic messengers, then those below them, etc.

The Infallibility of Prophets and Angels
Defines 'isma with linguistic and technical meanings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of 'isma (infallibility) for prophets and angels, its linguistic and technical meanings, and why it is obligatory to believe in it.

Core Idea
Infallibility is a divine grace that preserves prophets and angels from sin while preserving free will.

This lesson introduces the key theological concept of 'isma (infallibility). The passage defines what it means for prophets and angels to be protected from sin, both in language and in technical kalam terms. Understanding this definition is essential for grasping the Islamic doctrine of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the English translation. Notice the structure: first the obligation, then the definition.
The passage begins with an interspersed commentary style; focus on the core definitions.
2
Identify the two definitions of 'isma
Find the linguistic definition ('prevention') and the technical definition (Allah does not create sin while preserving ability and free will). Compare them.
The technical definition is more detailed and includes the preservation of free will.
3
Understand the explanation as a divine grace
Read the last part: 'isma is a lutf (grace) that inclines the servant to good and restrains from evil, while free will remains to make the trial meaningful. Reflect on why free will is preserved.
This balances divine protection with human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عصمة الأنبياء
(وَعِصْمَةُ البَارِي) أي: الخالق (لِكُلٍّ) أي: لكلِّ واحدٍ مِن الأنبياء
قسم النبوات
والملائكة دون غيرهم من الآحاد (حَتَّما) في الاعتقادِ على كلِّ مكلَّف(١) ، مِن كلِّ . يُنقص مَقامَهم من حركة أو سكون أو قول أو فعل. والعصمة لغة: المنع ، واصطلاحا: أن لا يخلق الله في المكلَّف الذَّنْب معَ بقاء قدرته (٢) واختياره، وهو معنى قولهم: «هي لطف من الله تعالى بالعبد ، يَحمِلُه على فعل الخير ، ويَزجُره عن الشَّرِّ ، مع بقاء الاختيار تحقيقا للابتلاء» (٣).
Protection of the Prophets
(And the protection of the Creator) meaning: the Creator (for every) meaning: for every one of the prophets
Section on Prophethoods
and the angels, not others of individuals, (definitely) in belief upon every morally responsible person, from everything that diminishes their station, whether movement or stillness, speech or action. And 'isma linguistically is: prevention; and technically: that Allah does not create sin in the morally responsible person while his ability and free will remain. And that is the meaning of their statement: 'It is a grace from Allah, the Exalted, to the servant, which impels him to do good and restrains him from evil, while free will remains to actualize the trial.'
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'isma (infallibility) for prophets and angels. It begins by stating that it is obligatory to believe that Allah protects every prophet and angel from anything that would diminish their station, whether in movement, stillness, speech, or action. Then it gives the linguistic and technical definitions: linguistically, 'isma means prevention; technically, it means that Allah does not create sin in the person while preserving their ability and free will. The passage explains that this is like a divine grace (lutf) that inclines the servant towards good and restrains from evil, but free will remains intact to make the trial meaningful.

Key Terms
عصمة
لطف
ذنب
قدرة
اختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'isma means prophets cannot sin at all by compulsion, as if Allah removes their ability to sin.
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'isma is a divine grace that preserves free will. Allah does not create sin in them, but they still have the ability and choice to sin, though by grace they do not.

Checkpoint
What is the technical definition of 'isma according to the passage?
A) That Allah prevents sin by removing free will
B) That Allah does not create sin in the person while preserving ability and free will
C) That the prophet is made incapable of sin
D) That sin is impossible for a prophet by nature

Key Takeaway
Infallibility ('isma) is a divine grace that prevents prophets and angels from committing sin while preserving their free will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says free will remains to actualize the trial. Are you treating your daily trials as opportunities to choose obedience to Allah, or do you often complain and wish the trial away? How would your response change if you saw each trial as a chance to prove your loyalty?
?
If you knew that Allah's grace could prevent you from sinning, would you still want to have free will? Or would you prefer compulsion? How does that affect your gratitude for the test He has given you?

Special Distinctions of Prophet Muhammad
Sanusi enumerates two special distinctions of Prophet Muhammad and notes their abundance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Prophet Muhammad was granted unique distinctions, particularly the finality and non-abrogation of his prophetic law, and that his distinctions are beyond enumeration.

Core Idea
Prophet Muhammad's law is the final, universal message for all time.

This lesson highlights the unique status of Prophet Muhammad among all prophets. The poem emphasizes that through him, Allah completed all goodness and made his law universal, never to be superseded. The commentary reminds us that these distinctions are countless.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the poem and its literal translation carefully. Notice the key phrase 'his law is not abrogated by another'.
The poem is concise; each line carries deep meaning.
2
Identify the two main distinctions
The passage mentions two specific honors: (1) completion of all good through him, and (2) his law is universal and never abrogated.
3
Understand the commentary's expansion
The commentary clarifies that 'best of creation' refers to Prophet Muhammad, and that his distinctions are countless (lā yanḥaṣiru).
This guards against thinking only these two distinctions exist.

The Definition of 'Isma (Infallibility)
The author defines 'isma linguistically and terminologically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and terminological definition of 'isma (infallibility) as a divine grace that preserves free will.

Core Idea
Infallibility means God withholds sin, not that prophets cannot sin.

This lesson introduces the definition of 'isma, a key concept in prophethood. The author clarifies both the linguistic and technical meanings, emphasizing that infallibility does not negate human free will. Understanding this definition prevents common misunderstandings about prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to get the literal meaning.
Notice the contrast between linguistic and terminological definitions.
2
Distinguish linguistic vs technical meaning
Identify that linguistically 'isma means 'prevention', while terminologically it means that God does not create sin in the mukallaf while ability and choice remain.
The technical definition builds on the linguistic one.
3
Understand the role of choice in trial
The passage explains that 'isma is a grace (lutf) that compels good and deters evil, but choice remains for the trial (ibtilā') to be genuine.
This clarifies that infallibility does not eliminate free will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعصمة لغة: المنع ، واصطلاحا: أن لا يخلق الله في المكلَّف الذَّنْب معَ بقاء قدرته واختياره، وهو معنى قولهم: «هي لطف من الله تعالى بالعبد ، يَحمِلُه على فعل الخير ، ويَزجُره عن الشَّرِّ ، مع بقاء الاختيار تحقيقا للابتلاء»
And 'isma (infallibility) lexically is prevention, and terminologically is that God does not create sin in the morally responsible person while his ability and choice remain, and it is the meaning of their statement: 'It is a grace from God Most High to the servant, compelling him to do good and deterring him from evil, while choice remains for the realization of trial.'
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'isma (infallibility) as it applies to prophets. The author first gives the linguistic meaning: prevention. Then the technical meaning: that God does not create sin in the morally responsible person (al-mukallaf) while preserving his ability and free choice. This definition emphasizes that infallibility does not remove the capacity to sin, but rather God withholds creating the sin. The author then equates this with another definition: that it is a divine grace (lutf) that impels the servant to good and deters him from evil, while choice remains intact to make the trial (ibtilā') genuine. This guards against the misunderstanding that infallibility negates human free will.

Key Terms
عصمة
مكلَّف
لطف
ابتلاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'isma means prophets cannot sin even if they try.
Correction: The definition clarifies that God does not create sin while the prophet retains ability and choice.

Checkpoint
What is the terminological definition of 'isma according to this passage?
A) That God removes the ability to sin from the prophet.
B) That God does not create sin in the mukallaf while his ability and choice remain.
C) That God forces the prophet to do good.
D) That the prophet has no free will.

Key Takeaway
The definition of 'isma shows that prophets are infallible by God's grace, yet retain free will, making their obedience meaningful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If the prophets, with full free will and divine grace, never sinned, why do you excuse your own sins by saying 'I'm only human'? Is it possible you are relying on God's mercy while ignoring His expectation of struggle? What is one sin you have normalized that you now see is an insult to the grace He offers?

Seal of Prophethood and Universal Mission
The author enumerates two special qualities of Prophet Muhammad with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two special qualities of Prophet Muhammad: the sealing of prophethood and the universality of his mission, along with their logical implications.

Core Idea
Prophet Muhammad sealed all prophethood and was sent to all beings.

This passage from Jawharat al-Tawhid highlights two distinctive honors bestowed upon Prophet Muhammad. The first is that he is the final prophet, through whom God completed and sealed all prophethood. The second is that his mission was made universal, encompassing all morally responsible beings. These two qualities establish the finality and universality of his message.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic matn and the commentator's explanation together with the literal translation. Let the author's own words set the foundation.
Notice the concise style of the matn and how the commentator expands each point.
2
Understand the Seal of Prophethood
The first quality: our Lord completed all prophethood through Muhammad. This means he is the 'Seal of the Prophets'. Understand why this also implies he is the seal of messengers.
The Quranic verse 33:40 is cited as evidence.
3
Understand the Universal Mission
The second quality: his mission was made universal in time and space. He was sent to all morally responsible beings: humans, jinn, Gog and Magog, and angels.
This establishes the universal scope of Islam.
4
Reflect on implications
Consider why no new prophethood or law can come after him, and how the return of Jesus (peace be upon him) will be under Muhammad's sharia.
This resolves a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخُصّ خيرُ الخلق أنْ قد تَمَّمَا به الجميعَ ربُّنا وعمَّما بِعَثَتَهُ فشرعُهُ لا يُنْسَخُ بغيره حتَّى الزَّمانُ يُنْسَخُ . قال الشارح: (وَخُصَّ خَيْرُ الخَلْقِ) أي خَصَّ اللهُ أفضلهم وهو نبينا محمَّد صلى الله عليه وسلم عَن سائرهم بما لا ينحصر حدا ولا عدا، ولكنَّ المُهمَّ منه أَنْ قَدْ تَمَّما بِه الجَمِيعَ رَبُّنَا أي خَتم ربُّنا بنبوته جميع الأنبياء، قال تعالى: ﴿وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّنَ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٠] . ويلزمُ منه ختم المرسلين أيضًا ؛ لأنَّ ختم الأعم ختم للأخص، من غير عكس فلا تُبْتِدَأُ نبوَّة ولا شريعة بعده. (وَعَمَّمَا) أي: وخُصَّ أيضًا بأنَّ ربَّنا عَمَّم (بِعْثَتْهُ) صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي الزَّمان والمكان ؛ فأرسله إلى جميع المُكلَّفين من الإنس والجن إجماعاً، ويأجوج ومأجوج والملائكة.
And the best of creation was singled out that our Lord completed all through him and made universal his mission, so his law is not abrogated by another until time is abrogated. The commentator said: 'And the best of creation was singled out' meaning God singled out the best of them, our Prophet Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, over others with what cannot be confined by limit or count, but the important of it is that our Lord completed all through him, i.e., our Lord sealed all prophets with his prophethood, as He said: 'And the Seal of the Prophets' [Quran 33:40]. And from that follows the sealing of messengers as well, because sealing the more general (prophets) entails sealing the more specific (messengers), without the reverse, so no prophethood or law is initiated after him. 'And made universal' means he was also singled out that our Lord made his mission universal in time and space; so he sent him to all morally responsible beings of humans and jinn by consensus, and to Gog and Magog and angels.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage explains two special qualities (khaṣā’iṣ) of Prophet Muhammad from the matn of Jawharat al-Tawhid. The matn verses state that he was singled out: (1) as the one through whom God completed all prophethood, and (2) as the one whose mission was universalized. The commentator clarifies each point. For the first, 'completing all' means that God sealed all prophets with Muhammad's prophethood, citing the Quranic verse 'Seal of the Prophets' (al-Ahzab 40). This logically entails that he is also the seal of messengers, since the category 'prophets' is wider than 'messengers'. Thus no new prophecy or revealed law can come after him. For the second, 'made universal' means that Muhammad was sent to all responsible beings—humans, jinn, Gog and Magog, and even angels—in all times and places. This establishes the universality and finality of his message.

Key Terms
خاتم النبيين
عمَّم
شرع
إرسال
مكلَّفين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the return of Jesus (peace be upon him) means a new prophethood or abrogation of Muhammad's law.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Muhammad is the seal of all prophets and messengers, so no new law comes after him. When Jesus returns, he will rule by the sharia of Muhammad.

Checkpoint
What is a necessary implication of Muhammad being the seal of the prophets?
A) He is also the seal of the messengers.
B) He was sent only to the Arabs.
C) His sharia is valid only until Jesus returns.
D) Angels are not obligated to follow his sharia.

Key Takeaway
Prophet Muhammad is the seal of all prophets and messengers, and his message is universal for all beings until the end of time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does this expand your understanding of your own responsibility to convey Islam to others, even those who seem 'different' from you? What specific step will you take this week to share something of this message with someone you usually avoid?
?
You read that no new law can come after Muhammad. Which command of the Quran or Sunnah have you been postponing, thinking you can obey it 'later'? What is the real cost of delaying your obedience, and what will you do to obey it now?

Was the Prophet Sent to Angels?
The author presents two scholarly opinions on whether the Prophet was sent to angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly opinions regarding whether the Prophet Muhammad was sent to angels, and the key scholars associated with each view.

Core Idea
The sending of the Prophet to angels is a matter of scholarly disagreement, not consensus.

This passage introduces a debated issue in Islamic theology: did the Prophet's mission extend to angels? The author presents two positions, each supported by notable scholars, showing that this question is not settled.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the English translation. Notice the structure: it first states there are two opinions, then details each.
2
Identify the two opinions
The first opinion says he was not sent to angels; the second says he was. Note the scholars who support each side.
Al-Bayhaqi and others support the first; al-Suyuti and al-Subki support the second.
3
Observe the extensions
Some proponents of the second opinion extended the mission to animals, inanimate objects, and even to the Prophet himself. Reflect on how this broadens the concept of prophethood.
Al-Barizi added animals and objects; al-Suyuti added 'sent to himself'.
4
Consider the significance
This disagreement shows that not all theological questions are settled. Understanding the range of opinions helps appreciate the diversity in Islamic thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف العلماء في إرساله إلى الملائكة على قولين: أحدهما: لم يكن مرسلا إليهم، وبهذا جزم الحلمي والبيهقي من الشافعية، ومحمد بن حمزة الكرماني في كتابه: «العجائب والغرائب من الحنفية، بل ونقل البرهان النسفي والفخر الرازي في تفسيريهما الإجماع عليه، وجزَم به مِن المُتأخرين زين الدين العراقي في نكته على ابن الصلاح ، والجلال المحلي في شرح جمع الجوامع». وثانيهما: أنه مبعوث إليهم ، وهذا القول رجحه الجلال السيوطي في خصائصه ، ورجحه قبله تقي الدين السبكي، وزاد أنه مرسل إلى الأنبياء والأمم السابقة . البارزي ، وزاد أنه مرسل إلى جميع الحيوانات والجمادات ، واستدل على ذلك بشهادة الضب له بالرسالة، وبشهادة الحجر والشجر له أيضا بذلك ، قال الجلال السيوطي: وأزيد إلى ذلك أنه مُرسل لنفسه. [أي مُكلف بأن يؤمن بأنه رسول من الله ] . انظر: «هداية المريد ج ٢ ص ٨٢١ وما بعدها»
And the scholars differed regarding his sending to the angels into two opinions: One: He was not sent to them, and this was asserted by al-Hulaymi and al-Bayhaqi from the Shafi'is, and Muhammad ibn Hamza al-Kirmani in his book 'al-Aja'ib wa al-Ghara'ib' from the Hanafis, and al-Burhan al-Nasafi and Fakhr al-Razi in their two commentaries transmitted consensus upon it, and it was asserted by later scholars like Zayn al-Din al-Iraqi in his critical notes on Ibn al-Salah, and al-Jalal al-Mahalli in his commentary on Jam' al-Jawami'. And the second: That he was sent to them, and this opinion was favored by al-Jalal al-Suyuti in his Khasais, and favored before him by Taqi al-Din al-Subki, and he added that he is sent to the prophets and previous nations. Al-Barizi added that he is sent to all animals and inanimate objects, and he adduced for that the testimony of the lizard to his prophethood, and the testimony of the stone and the tree also for that. Al-Jalal al-Suyuti said: And I add to that that he is sent to himself. (i.e., obligated to believe that he is a messenger from God). See: Hidaya al-Murid vol. 2 p. 821 and onwards.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage presents a scholarly disagreement on whether the Prophet was sent to angels. The author classifies the issue into two opinions: (1) He was not sent to them, asserted by many scholars including al-Hulaymi, al-Bayhaqi, al-Kirmani, and others, with some claiming consensus. (2) He was sent to them, favored by al-Suyuti and al-Subki, with expansions by al-Barizi (sending to animals and objects) and al-Suyuti adding that he is sent to himself. The author follows the natural order of the two positions, citing names and justifications, and ends with a reference to further reading. The passage is a classification and enumeration of a known kalam disagreement, not a resolution.

Key Terms
إرساله إلى الملائكة
قولين
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All scholars agree that the Prophet was sent to angels.
Correction: This passage shows a clear disagreement: many scholars held he was not sent to angels, and some claimed consensus on that view.

Checkpoint

B) Al-Bayhaqi
C) Taqi al-Din al-Subki

Key Takeaway
The question of whether the Prophet was sent to angels is not settled in Islamic scholarship; there are two distinct positions with authoritative backing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Universality of the Prophet's Mission
The author states the universal scope of the Prophet's message and cites a Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet Muhammad was sent to all creation, including angels, animals, inanimate objects, and even himself, as stated in the Quran.

Core Idea
The Prophet's mission extends to everything in existence.

This lesson establishes a foundational principle of Islamic theology: the universal scope of the Prophet's message. The author begins by enumerating the recipients of his mission, including angels, animals, and inanimate objects, and even includes the Prophet's own soul. This is supported by a clear Quranic verse that states he was sent comprehensively to all mankind.

Guided Path
1
Read the statement of universality
Read the Arabic sentence carefully. Note the progression from angels to animals to inanimate objects, and finally to the Prophet himself.
The phrase 'even to himself' highlights that the Prophet must acknowledge his own prophethood.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
The verse from Surah Saba is cited as the primary proof. Reflect on the word 'kaffatan' (comprehensively) and its implications.
3
Consider the rationale
Think about why it is important that the Prophet was sent to all of creation. The commentary elaborates on the benefit for animals and inanimate objects.
The commentary mentions that animals are safe from punishment and inanimate objects can be endowed with perception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إرساله إلى الملائكة الحيوانات والجمادات(۱) ، حتَّى إلى نفسه (۲)، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَاكَ إِلَّا كَافَةً لِلنَّاسِ (سبأ: ۲۸) وفيه ردُّ على العيسوية (۳) من اليهود حيثُ (۱) قوله: (وجميع الحيوانات والجمادات والإرسال إلى الحيوانات نجاة وأمان من الخسف والمَسخ ، فقد كان يُخْسِفُ بها في الأمم الماضية ، وقوله : ( والجمادات) أي: فآمنت به ، ولا مانع من أن الله يودعها الإدراك ، وفائدة ذلك أنها صارت مأمونة مِن أنْ تُساقَ إلى جهنم ويعذب بها أهلها، فحجارة جهنم هي غير الحجارة التي على ظهر الدنيا، فإن قلت: من جملة الجمادات الأصنام، وقد ورد أنها تُدخل مع عُبَادِها ، فالجوب: أنها وإن دخلتها لكن لا يعذب بها ، فدخولها للتنكيل عليهم الشنواني . (۳) العيسوية من يهود أصبهان، نسبوا إلى أبي عيسى إسحاق بن يعقوب الأصفهاني. وقيل: إن اسمه: عوفيد ألوهيم أي عابد الله . كان في زمن المنصور، وابتدأ دعوته في زمن آخر ملوك بني أمية مروان بن محمد الحمار ، فاتبعه بشرٌ كثير من اليهود، وادعوا له آيات ومعجزات ، زعم أبو عيسى أنه نبي ؛ وأنه رسول المسيح المنتظر . وزعم أن للمسيح خمسة من الرسل يأتون قبله واحدا بعد واحد وهو آخرهم. وزعم أن الله تعالى كلمه، وكلَّفَهُ أَنْ يُخلص بني إسرائيل من أيدي الأمم العاصين والملوك الظالمين. وزعم أن المسيح أفضل ولد آدم، وأنه أعلى منزلة من الأنبياء الماضين، وإذ هو رسوله فهو أفضل الكل أيضا، وخالف اليهود في كثير من أحكام الشريعة الكثيرة المذكورة في التوراة. وقد حارب المسلمين وقتل كثيرا منهم ، والعيسوية يقرُّونَ بنبوة نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وبأن كل ما جاء به حق ؛ ولكنهم زعموا أنه بعث إلى العرب خاصة لا إلى بني إسرائيل. انظر: «الفرق بين الفرق» و«الملل والنحل . فائدة: ردَّ الإمام حجة الإسلام الغزالي على زعم العيسوية فقال في كتابه «الاقتصاد في الاعتقاد حيث ذهبوا إلى أنه الرسول إلى العرب فقط لا إلى غيرهم، وهذا ظاهر البطلان ؛ فإنهم اعترفوا بكونه رسولا حقا، ومعلوم أن الرسول لا يكذب، وقد ادعى هو أنه رسول مبعوث إلى الثقلين ، وبَعثَ رُسُله إلى كسرى وقيصر وسائر ملوك العجم، وتواتر ذلك منه ، فما قالوه محال متناقض). قسم النبوات زعموا تخصيص رسالته بالعرب ، ومَن نفى بعثته كُلًّا أو بعضا (۱) كَمَن نفى الإسلام كذلك فهو كافر عند الأشاعرة (۲) إن كان مُكلَّفا وبلغته الدعوة (۱) قوله: (كلا) أي: إن أنكر بعثته من أصلها وقوله : (أو بعضا) أي: بشرط أن يكون معلوماً من الدين بالضرورة. الشنواني . (٢) أي عند أهل السنة مطلقا . الشنواني .
His sending to the angels, animals, and inanimate objects (1), even to himself (2), and His statement Exalted is He: “And We have not sent you except comprehensively to mankind” [Saba: 28]; and in it is a refutation of the ‘Isawiyya (3) from the Jews, who (1) His statement: “and all the animals and inanimate objects – and sending to the animals is deliverance and safety from being swallowed and metamorphosed, for that used to happen to them in past nations, and His statement: ‘and inanimate objects’ means: so they believed in him, and there is no impediment to Allah endowing them with perception, and the benefit of that is that they become safe from being driven to Hell and its inhabitants being punished by them, for the stones of Hell are other than the stones on the surface of the earth; if you say: among the inanimate objects are idols, and it has come that they are entered with their worshippers, the answer is: that even if they enter it, they are not punished by them, for their entry is for humiliation upon them – al-Shanwani. (2) His statement: “even to himself” meaning that he must necessarily acknowledge that he is the Messenger of Allah, verified by miracles – al-Shanwani. (3) The ‘Isawiyya are from the Jews of Isfahan, traced to Abu ‘Isa Ishaq ibn Ya‘qub al-Isfahani. It is said his name was ‘Ufayd Aluhim, i.e., servant of Allah. He was in the time of al-Mansur, and began his call in the time of the last Umayyad kings Marwan ibn Muhammad al-Himar, and many Jews followed him, and they claimed for him signs and miracles. Abu ‘Isa claimed that he was a prophet, and that he was the messenger of the awaited Messiah. He claimed that the Messiah has five messengers who come before him one after another, and he is the last of them. He claimed that Allah spoke to him and charged him to deliver the Children of Israel from the hands of the disobedient nations and oppressive kings. He claimed that the Messiah is the best of the children of Adam, and that he is of higher station than the past prophets, and since he is his messenger, he is also the best of all. He opposed the Jews in many of the many rulings of the law mentioned in the Torah. He fought the Muslims and killed many of them. The ‘Isawiyya affirm the prophethood of our Prophet Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) and that everything he brought is true, but they claimed that he was sent specifically to the Arabs, not to the Children of Israel. See: “al-Farq bayn al-Firaq” and “al-Milal wa al-Nihal”. Benefit: The Imam, Proof of Islam, al-Ghazali, refuted the claim of the ‘Isawiyya and said in his book “al-Iqtisad fi al-I‘tiqad” where they held that he is the messenger only to the Arabs, not to others, and this is manifest falsehood; for they acknowledged that he is truly a messenger, and it is known that a messenger does not lie, and he claimed that he is a messenger sent to the two weighty ones (humans and jinn), and he sent his messengers to Kisra and Caesar and the rest of the kings of the non-Arabs, and that is mutawatir from him, so what they said is impossible and contradictory. Section on Prophethoods. They claimed the specification of his message to the Arabs, and whoever denies his mission entirely or partially (1) is like whoever denies Islam likewise, so he is a disbeliever according to the Ash‘aris (2) if he is legally responsible and the call reached him. (1) His statement: “entirely” i.e., if he denies his mission from its origin, and his statement “or partially” i.e., on condition that it is known necessarily from the religion – al-Shanwani. (2) i.e., according to Ahl al-Sunna absolutely – al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part refutation and ruling. First, it asserts the universal scope of the Prophet’s mission: it includes angels, animals, inanimate objects, and even himself (meaning his own soul must acknowledge his prophethood). The verse from Surah Saba is cited as evidence: “We have not sent you except comprehensively to mankind.” The author then identifies the opposing group, the ‘Isawiyya (a Jewish sect from Isfahan), providing a detailed account of their founder Abu ‘Isa and their beliefs. The key point is that they accept the Prophet’s prophethood but restrict it to Arabs, claiming he was not sent to the Children of Israel. This is refuted by Imam al-Ghazali, who argues that since they admit he is a true messenger, and he himself claimed universality (sent to both humans and jinn) and acted on it by sending letters to royalty, their position is self-contradictory. The passage then moves to a doctrinal ruling: whoever denies the Prophet’s mission in whole or in part (where the part is known necessarily from religion) is a disbeliever according to the Ash‘aris (i.e., Ahl al-Sunna). The footnotes clarify that “partially” means what is known by necessity, and the ruling applies if the person is legally responsible and the call has reached them.

Key Terms
عموم الرسالة
كافرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the Prophet was sent only to humans, excluding angels, animals, and jinn.
Correction: The passage explicitly includes angels, animals, inanimate objects, and even the Prophet himself, showing the mission encompasses all of creation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, to which of the following was the Prophet sent?
A) Humans only
B) Humans and jinn
C) Angels, animals, inanimate objects, and himself
D) Only Arabs

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad was sent to all creation, not just humans.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet was sent to inanimate objects, how does that affect your treatment of the material world around you? Do you see your phone, your car, or your home as part of that mission? What changes if you do?
?
The Prophet was sent even to himself. Are you as strict in holding yourself accountable to his teachings as you are with others? Where do you make exceptions for yourself that you wouldn’t accept from someone else?
?
The verse says the Prophet was sent 'comprehensively to mankind.' If you truly believed that, would you be content with your current efforts to share Islam? When did you last speak to someone who isn't Muslim with the conviction that this message is for them? What stops you?

Prophethood
intermediate
10 min
Refuting the 'Isawiyya: The Universality of the Message
The author describes the 'Isawiyya sect and presents al-Ghazali's refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the beliefs of the 'Isawiyya sect and the refutation by Imam al-Ghazali based on the Prophet’s own claims and actions.

Core Idea
Those who accept the Prophet but restrict his mission contradict his own declarations.

This lesson introduces a historical sect that acknowledged the Prophet’s prophethood but limited it to Arabs. The author provides a detailed description of the 'Isawiyya and then presents al-Ghazali’s logical refutation: since the Prophet claimed universality and acted on it, restricting his message is self-contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Learn about the 'Isawiyya
Read the description of this Jewish sect from Isfahan, their founder Abu 'Isa, and their beliefs. Note that they accept the Prophet’s prophethood but confine it to Arabs.
2
Understand al-Ghazali's refutation
Al-Ghazali argues that if they acknowledge he is a true messenger, then he cannot lie. Since he claimed to be sent to both humans and jinn, and sent letters to kings, their position is impossible.
The refutation is from his book 'al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad'.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Consider why this refutation is important for establishing the universal scope of the message.

What was the main claim of the 'Isawiyya regarding the Prophet Muhammad?
A) He was not a prophet

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the Prophet's message is for every human being and jinn, including those you dislike or consider different? Or have you unconsciously restricted his mission to your own circle? Pledge today to actively share or embody the universality of his message.
?
When you claim to follow the Prophet, do you accept all his claims, including the universality of his prophethood, or do you privately limit his authority to certain areas of life? Confess any areas where you've been selective and commit to full submission.
?
If the 'Isawiyya's error was to restrict the Prophet's message to a group, have you ever restricted it to a time, place, or aspect of your life? What step will you take this week to live out the all-encompassing nature of his teaching?

Prophethood
