?
The Prophet is first in everything good—first to be resurrected, first at the gathering, first in Paradise. You claim to follow him, but are you competing to be first in good deeds, or are you content to be last? What one deed will you begin today to imitate his priority?
?
Imagine standing in that vast gathering, watching the Prophet arrive first while you are far behind. What would you say to him if he asked about your effort in this life? Write a truthful answer now, as if you were already there.

Three Obligatory Beliefs About the Prophet
Enumeration of three obligatory beliefs about the Prophet's intercession and rank.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three obligatory beliefs regarding the Prophet's intercession and his precedence over all creation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession and rank are matters of necessary belief.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid introduces three essential beliefs about the Prophet that every Muslim must hold. These are not optional opinions but obligatory doctrines rooted in revelation. Let's examine each one.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation once to get an overview of the three beliefs listed.
Notice the sequence: shafi', mushaffa', muqaddam.
2
Identify the three beliefs
List each of the three beliefs in your own words: the Prophet is an intercessor, his intercession is accepted, and he is given precedence over all others.
The text explicitly calls these obligatory upon every legally responsible person.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these beliefs are placed under 'Sam'iyyat' (matters heard from revelation) and why they are obligatory. What would be missing if one denied any of them?
This shows that the Prophet's role in intercession is a confirmed part of Islamic creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات على كل مُكلَّف: فالأول : كونه صلى الله عليه وسلم شَافِعًا. والثَّاني : كونه صلى الله عليه وسلم مُشَفعًا ، أي : مَقبُولَ الشفاعة. والثالث : كونه مُقَدَّمًا على غيره مِن جميع الأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة المقربين.
Section of the Sam'iyyat (matters heard from revelation). Upon every legally responsible person: the first: that he, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is an intercessor; the second: that he is one whose intercession is accepted, meaning: accepted intercession; and the third: that he is given precedence over others among all the prophets, messengers, and the near angels.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of three obligatory beliefs that fall under the section of Sam'iyyat. The commentator states that it is incumbent upon every legally responsible person to believe: firstly, that the Prophet Muhammad is an intercessor (shafi'); secondly, that his intercession is accepted (mushaffa'), meaning that it is not rejected; and thirdly, that he is given precedence (muqaddam) over all other prophets, messengers, and the most honored angels. These three points establish the Prophet's unique status regarding intercession and rank.

Key Terms
شفاعة
مشفع
مقدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet's intercession is only for major sinners or that it is not necessary to believe in intercession.
Correction: The passage clarifies that believing in the Prophet's intercession and its acceptance is obligatory for every Muslim, and it is a general belief about his status, not limited to any group.

Checkpoint
What are the three obligatory beliefs mentioned about the Prophet in this passage?
A) He is a prophet, messenger, and seal of prophets
B) He is an intercessor, his intercession is accepted, and he is given precedence over all others
C) He is the best of creation, his intercession is for Muslims only, and he is sinless
D) He is intercessor, his intercession is for believers only, and he is preferred over angels

Key Takeaway
Every Muslim must believe that the Prophet is an intercessor, his intercession is accepted, and he holds the highest rank among all creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage declares these beliefs obligatory. Have you ever acted as if they were optional? What would change in your life if you lived every moment with the certainty that the Prophet is the intercessor, his intercession is accepted, and he is the highest of all creation?

The Grand Intercession: Relief from the Standing
The commentator describes the first type of intercession: the grand intercession for relief from the standing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature and purpose of the Prophet’s grand intercession, which is unique to him and provides relief from the long standing on the Day of Resurrection.

Core Idea
The Prophet's grand intercession is his unique gift to relieve humanity from the anguish of the standing.

In this short but dense passage, the commentator introduces the first and greatest of the Prophet’s intercessions. He makes clear that this intercession is exclusively for the Prophet (peace be upon him) and that its specific purpose is to bring relief from the prolonged waiting of the Day of Judgment. This intercession is identified as the beginning of the Praiseworthy Station mentioned in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the original Arabic and the English translation once to get the overall meaning.
Notice the word 'تعيّن' (it is necessary) indicating obligation in belief.
2
Analyze the first part
The commentator states that the Prophet has many intercessions, but the greatest is the grand intercession, unique to him.
This establishes the distinction between general intercessions and this special one.
3
Understand the purpose
The intercession is for relief from the length of the standing (al-mawqif). This refers to the long wait on the Day of Resurrection before judgment.
4
Connect to the Praiseworthy Station
The intercession is identified as the first aspect of al-maqam al-mahmud (Quran 17:79), showing its Quranic basis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيَتعيّنُ اعتقاد أنَّ له شَفاعات إلَّا أنَّ أعظمها : شفاعته العُظْمَى المختصَّةُ به؛ للإراحة مِن طُول المَوقِف، وهي: أوّل المقام المحمود.
It is necessary to believe that he has intercessions, except that the greatest of them is his grand intercession unique to him, for relief from the length of the standing, and it is the first of the Praiseworthy Station (al-maqam al-mahmud).
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage defines the first and greatest of the Prophet's intercessions. The commentator asserts that it is obligatory to believe that the Prophet has many intercessions, but the greatest one is his 'grand intercession' which is exclusively his. This intercession occurs for the purpose of relief from the long wait of the standing on the Day of Resurrection. He identifies this intercession as the first aspect of the Praiseworthy Station (al-maqam al-mahmud) mentioned in the Quran (17:79). The commentator implies that this intercession is universally accepted among scholars.

The Prophet’s grand intercession is his unique role to relieve the creation from the distress of the standing on the Day of Resurrection, and it is the first part of his Praiseworthy Station.

The Second Type: Intercession for Paradise Without Reckoning
Al-Nawawi's statement on the second type of intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second type of intercession — for a people to enter Paradise without reckoning — and that it is considered exclusive to the Prophet according to al-Nawawi.

Core Idea
The Prophet alone can intercede for some to enter Paradise without any prior reckoning.

After covering the first type of intercession, the commentator now lists the second type. This intercession involves the Prophet bringing a group of people directly into Paradise without any accounting of their deeds. Al-Nawawi explicitly states that this privilege is unique to the Prophet Muhammad. Let's examine the Arabic text to appreciate the phrasing and its theological weight.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic sentence for the second type slowly. Notice the key phrase 'إدخال الجنة بغير حساب' and the word 'مختصة' which indicates exclusivity.
2
Understand al-Nawawi's assertion
Al-Nawawi says this type is exclusive to the Prophet. Reflect on what 'exclusive' means for the power of the Prophet's intercession.
Exclusivity means no other prophet or saint shares this particular intercession.
3
Connect to the broader topic
Consider why this type is distinct from the first type (intercession for major sinners to be taken out of Hell). How are they similar? How are they different?
The first type involves people already in Hell; this second type involves people not entering the reckoning process at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيها: في إدخال قوم الجنَّةَ بغير حساب، وهي مختصة به فيما قاله النَّوويُّ. ثالثها: فيمن استحق دخول النار أن لا يدخلها، وتردَّد النَّوويُّ في اختصاصها به.
The second of them: regarding the entry of a people into Paradise without reckoning, and it is exclusive to him according to what al-Nawawi said. The third of them: regarding the one who deserves entry into the Fire that he should not enter it, and al-Nawawi hesitated regarding its exclusivity to him.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage presents two more types of intercession. The second type is intercession for some people to enter Paradise without any reckoning. According to al-Nawawi, this type is exclusive to the Prophet. The third type is intercession on behalf of someone who deserves to enter Hell, so that they are prevented from entering it. Regarding this third type, al-Nawawi expressed hesitation about whether it is exclusive to the Prophet or not, indicating some scholarly disagreement.

Key Terms
إدخال الجنة بغير حساب
مختصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that intercession for entering Paradise without reckoning is a general mercy available to any saint or prophet.
Correction: Al-Nawawi asserts that this specific type is exclusive to the Prophet Muhammad. The passage clearly states 'وهي مختصة به', meaning it is uniquely his.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nawawi, which type of intercession is exclusive to the Prophet?
A) Intercession for major sinners to leave Hell
B) Intercession for entering Paradise without reckoning
C) Intercession to prevent entry into Hell
D) Intercession for increasing degrees in Paradise

Key Takeaway
The second type of intercession is the Prophet's exclusive power to admit some people into Paradise without any reckoning, as stated by al-Nawawi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What does the Prophet's exclusive power to admit some into Paradise without reckoning reveal about his station? Are you living in a way that makes you yearn for that honorful intercession?
?
If you were to be among those who enter Paradise without reckoning, what would change in your daily priorities and fears? How does this hope shape your reliance on the Prophet today?

The Third Type: Intercession to Prevent Entry to Hell
Al-Nawawi's guarded statement on the third type of intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third type of intercession — for someone who deserves Hell to be kept out — and the uncertainty al-Nawawi expressed about its exclusivity.

Core Idea
Al-Nawawi hesitated whether the Prophet alone can intercede to prevent a deserving person from entering Hell.

The third type of intercession is for a person who has earned entry into the Fire, but intercession is made so that they never enter it at all. Unlike the second type, al-Nawawi did not definitively state that it is exclusive to the Prophet. Instead, he expressed hesitation. This opens a window into how scholars differ on the scope of prophetic intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic for the third type
Read the sentence carefully. Note the phrase 'فيمن استحق دخول النار أن لا يدخلها' and the word 'تردد' (hesitation).
2
Identify the key point of uncertainty
Al-Nawawi 'تردد' (hesitated) about whether this type is exclusive to the Prophet. This means he did not lean definitively one way or the other. What might be the reason for this hesitation?
Hesitation indicates there are valid arguments on both sides.
3
Compare with the second type
Contrast this hesitation with the clear statement of exclusivity for the second type. How does the language differ? What does that tell us about the scholarly treatment of these two types?
The second type had 'وهي مختصة به' (it is exclusive to him), while the third has 'تردد النووي في اختصاصها به' (al-Nawawi hesitated in its exclusivity).

The Prophet's Exclusive Intercession for Minimal Faith
The commentator explains the fourth type and al-Qadi 'Iyad's distinction on exclusivity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth type of intercession and the condition under which it is exclusive to the Prophet.

Core Idea
The Prophet's exclusive intercession is for those with only a mustard seed of faith.

The commentator now turns to the fourth type of intercession: bringing monotheists out of Hellfire. While many can intercede for believers with some good deeds, there is a specific case where only the Prophet's intercession avails. Al-Qadi 'Iyad provides a crucial distinction that clarifies this exclusivity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without rushing. Then read the literal translation. Focus on the overall structure: first a general statement, then a detailed condition.
2
Identify the two parts
Notice that the passage begins by stating the fourth type and listing its co-participants (prophets, angels, believers). Then it quotes al-Qadi 'Iyad who gives a conditional distinction.
The conditional is 'إن كانت... وإلا' (if... otherwise).
3
Analyze the condition
Al-Qadi 'Iyad says: if the intercession is for someone with only a mustard seed of faith (and no good deeds to rely on), then it is exclusive to the Prophet. If the person has more than that, others may also intercede.
4
Reflect on the significance
This shows that the Prophet has a unique role for the most helpless believers. It also teaches that intercession is not arbitrary; it depends on the person's state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعها: في إخراج الموحدين مِن النَّار، ويُشاركه في هذه الأنبياء والملائكة والمؤمنونَ، وفَصَّل القاضي عياض فقال: إن كانت هذه الشفاعة لإخراج من في قلبه مثقالُ ذَرَّةٍ مِن إيمان اختصت به ، ولا يُشاركه غيره، وإلَّا شارَكَهُ فيها غيره.
The fourth of them: regarding the extraction of monotheists from the Fire, and in this he is shared by the prophets, angels, and believers. And al-Qadi 'Iyad detailed saying: If this intercession is for the extraction of one who has in his heart the weight of a mustard seed of faith, then it is exclusive to him, and none other shares with him; otherwise, others share with him in it.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage describes the fourth type of intercession, which is concerning the removal of monotheists from Hellfire. The commentator notes that in this type, the Prophet is joined by other prophets, angels, and believers. However, al-Qadi 'Iyad provides a detailed distinction: if the intercession is for someone who has only the weight of a mustard seed of faith without any good deeds beyond that, then this intercession is exclusive to the Prophet; no one else shares it. But if the person has some good deeds in addition to faith, then others may also intercede for him. This shows a nuanced understanding of who can intercede and under what conditions.

Key Terms
إخراج الموحدين
مثقال ذرة
تفصيل القاضي عياض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think all intercession for removing from fire is exclusive to the Prophet.
Correction: It is exclusive only for those with minimal faith (mustard seed); otherwise, others also intercede.

Checkpoint
According to al-Qadi 'Iyad, when is the intercession for bringing monotheists out of the Fire exclusive to the Prophet?
A) Always exclusive
B) When the person has the weight of a mustard seed of faith and no good deeds
C) When the person is a great sinner
D) When the person repented

Key Takeaway
The fourth intercession is for removing monotheists from Hell, and only the Prophet can intercede for those with the smallest amount of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Fifth Type: Increasing Degrees in Paradise
Sanusi presents the fifth type: intercession for increasing ranks in Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth type of intercession—the Prophet's intercession to increase the ranks of the people of Paradise—and the scholarly opinion that it may be exclusive to him.

Core Idea
Intercession elevates believers' ranks in Paradise.

After covering intercession for entering Paradise, Sanusi now mentions an even higher gift: increasing degrees for those already there. This shows that the Prophet's intercession can benefit believers not only by admitting them but also by raising their status. Let's examine this type closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the fifth type
Carefully read the Arabic sentence and its translation. Notice that it specifies 'the fifth' and mentions al-Nawawi's view.
Al-Nawawi was a prominent Shafi'i scholar.
2
Identify the core benefit
This intercession is for increasing degrees, not for forgiveness or entry. It is an upgrade for those already in Paradise.
3
Understand the exclusive view
Al-Nawawi allowed the possibility that this type is exclusive to the Prophet, meaning no other prophet or saint shares this specific intercession.
This highlights the Prophet's unique status.
4
Reflect on why this matters
This type shows that intercession is not only remedial (saving from punishment) but also elevating (granting higher reward).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خَامِسُهَا: في زيادة الدرجات في الجنَّة لأهلها ، وجوز النَّوويُّ اختصاصها به . سادسُها في جماعةٍ مِن صُلحَاءِ أَمَّته ؛ ليتجاوز عنهم في تقصيرهم في الطاعات . سابعها: فيمن خُلد في النَّارِ مِن الكفر أن يخفف عنهم العذاب في أوقاتٍ مخصوصة كما في حق أبي طالب وأبي لهب.
The fifth of them: regarding the increase of degrees in Paradise for its inhabitants, and al-Nawawi allowed its exclusivity to him. The sixth of them: regarding a group of the righteous of his community, so that they be forgiven for their shortcomings in acts of obedience. The seventh of them: regarding those who are eternally in the Fire from disbelief, that the punishment be lightened for them at specific times, as in the case of Abu Talib and Abu Lahab.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage concludes the enumeration of the seven types of intercession with three more types. The fifth type is intercession for increasing the ranks of the people of Paradise. Al-Nawawi considered this type possibly exclusive to the Prophet. The sixth type is intercession for a group of the righteous among his community, so that their deficiencies in acts of obedience are overlooked. The seventh type is intercession for those who are permanently in Hell due to disbelief, to have their punishment lessened at specific times, as exemplified by Abu Talib and Abu Lahab. This demonstrates that the Prophet's intercession can benefit even some disbelievers in a limited way.

Key Terms
زيادة الدرجات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the fifth type of intercession involve?
A) Forgiving sins of the righteous
B) Increasing degrees in Paradise
C) Lightening punishment for disbelievers
D) Entering people into Paradise

Key Takeaway
The fifth intercession is a unique blessing that elevates believers' ranks in Paradise, possibly exclusive to the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Seventh Type: Lightening Punishment for Disbelievers
Sanusi presents the seventh type: intercession to lighten punishment for certain disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seventh type of intercession—the Prophet's intercession to lighten the punishment of certain disbelievers who are eternally in Hell, such as Abu Talib and Abu Lahab.

Core Idea
Even some disbelievers receive temporary relief through intercession.

The final type is the most surprising: intercession benefits even a few disbelievers. While they remain in Hell forever, their torment is reduced at specific times. Sanusi cites the examples of Abu Talib and Abu Lahab. This shows the vast reach of the Prophet's intercession. Let's study the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the seventh type
Read the Arabic sentence. Note 'فيمن خُلد في النَّارِ مِن الكفر' (regarding those who are eternally in the Fire from disbelief).
2
Identify the beneficiaries
They are disbelievers who are in Hell forever. But the intercession lightens their torment 'في أوقاتٍ مخصوصة' (at specific times).
3
Understand the examples
Abu Talib (the Prophet's uncle who did not accept Islam) and Abu Lahab (his hostile uncle) are given as examples. Both are in Hell, but receive reduced punishment at certain times due to the Prophet's intercession.
This is based on hadith.
4
Reflect on the limitation
This intercession does not remove them from Hell, only lessens the severity. It is not a general intercession for all disbelievers.

D) It allows them to enter Paradise

Key Takeaway
The seventh intercession shows that even disbelievers can receive temporary relief from punishment through the Prophet's mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever feel that your sins are so great that even the Prophet's intercession couldn't reach you? This lesson shows that even Abu Lahab, who opposed Islam, receives some relief. What does that say about the Prophet's mercy, and how should it change your hope in his intercession?
?
Abu Talib received lightening because he protected the Prophet. What have you done today to support the Prophet's legacy? Is it enough?
?
The lightening is only at specific times, not permanent. Are you satisfied with temporary relief from Allah's displeasure, or do you strive for full forgiveness? What are you doing to ensure you are not among those who only get temporary relief?

Eternal Blessings upon the Prophet of Mercy
Commentator explains the final line sending eternal prayers and peace upon the Prophet whose habit is mercy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the prayers and peace upon the Prophet are described as 'eternal' and what it means that his constant habit is mercy.

Core Idea
The Prophet's only habit is mercy; salawat are eternal in reward, not utterance.

This lesson unpacks the final line of Sanusi's poem, where he sends perpetual prayers and peace upon the Prophet. The commentator clarifies that 'eternal' refers to the lasting merit of these blessings, not their utterance. Moreover, the Prophet is described as one whose continuous custom is mercy—a profound description of his character.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: the phrase 'al-da'im' and its explanation.
The passage includes parentheses with commentary.
2
Understand 'eternal' correctly
The commentator says the eternal quality applies to the merit and fruit of salawat, not the utterance itself. Why? Because salawat are accidents that pass away as soon as spoken.
3
Examine 'dābahu al-marāḥim'
Break down the phrase: 'dāb' means continuous custom, 'marāḥim' is plural of mercy. The Prophet has no habit except mercy.
4
Reflect on the Prophet's mercy
Consider how this description encapsulates the Prophet's character. What does it mean that his very nature is mercy?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٤٣. ثُمَّ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ الدَّائِمُ عَلَى نَبِيٌّ دَابَهُ المَرَاحِمُ (ثُمَّ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ الدَّائِمُ كلُّ مِنهما، أي: الدَّائمُ فضلهما وثمرتُهما ؛ لأنهما عَرضَان ينقضيان بمُجرَّد النُّطْقِ بهما (عَلى نَبِيٌّ دَابَهُ) ، أي : عَادِتُه المُستمِرَّةُ (المَرَاحِمُ) الكاملة ، جمعُ مَرْحَمَةٍ، بمعنى الرُّحْم أو الرَّحْمَةِ(٤) ، والمعنى: ثُمَّ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ على نبي موصوف بأنَّهُ لا عادة له إلا المَرَاحِمُ ، أي : شِيمَتُه
143. Then the eternal prayer and peace be upon a prophet whose constant habit is mercies. (Then the prayer and the peace are eternal) each of them, meaning: their merit and fruit are eternal; because they are accidents that cease with merely uttering them. (Upon a prophet whose constant habit is) meaning: his continuous custom (mercies) the complete, plural of mercy (marhamah), meaning compassion or mercy. And the meaning: Then the prayer and peace be upon a prophet described that he has no habit except mercies, meaning: his disposition.
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage is the commentary on the final line of the poem (line 143), which sends perpetual prayers and peace upon the Prophet. The commentator explains that 'al-da'im' (the eternal) describes both prayer and peace, but this refers to the permanence of their merit and reward, because prayer and peace are accidents (a'rad) that pass away with the utterance. The phrase 'ala nabiyyin dābahu al-marāḥim' is broken down: 'dāb' means continuous custom, and 'marāḥim' (plural of marḥamah) means complete mercies, from the root raḥma (mercy/compassion). The overall meaning is that the Prophet's only constant habit is mercy. The commentator ends with 'ay shīmatuhu' (meaning his disposition). This emphasizes the Prophet's attribute of comprehensive and perpetual mercy.

Key Terms
الصلاة
السلام
النبي
المَرَاحِم
الدأب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'eternal' prayer means the actual utterance of salawat lasts forever.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that because salawat are accidents that cease with utterance, the eternity refers to their merit and reward.

Checkpoint
Why are the prayer and peace described as 'eternal' (al-da'im)?
A) Because the words themselves last forever
B) Because their merit and fruit are eternal
C) Because the Prophet recites them eternally
D) Because they are not subject to time

Key Takeaway
The eternal blessings on the Prophet have everlasting merit, and his defining attribute is mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's sole habit is mercy. In your own life, what is your most consistent habit? Is it mercy? If not, what specific action will you take today to make mercy your dāb?
?
When you send salawat on the Prophet, do you truly believe that its reward is eternal and far greater than the fleeting moment it takes to utter it? How does that belief change the way you say it?

The Perpetual Blessings on the Prophet of Mercy
Explanation of the closing line invoking blessings on the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rationale for framing a book with blessings on the Prophet, the perpetual nature of those blessings, and the profound meaning of the Prophet's habit of mercy as connected to Quran 21:107.

Core Idea
The Prophet's very character is mercy, and blessings upon him are perpetual in effect.

The commentator explains the closing line of a poem invoking blessings and peace on the Prophet. He shows why the poet framed his work with these blessings, clarifies that the blessings are perpetual despite being transient utterances, and unpacks the phrase 'daabuhu al-marahim'—the Prophet's unceasing habit of mercy. This leads to a powerful connection with the Qur'anic verse that describes the Prophet as a mercy to all worlds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once for rhythm, then the translation. Notice the commentator's explanation of why blessings open and close the book.
The passage contains a quote from the poem being explained.
2
Understand the framing of blessings
The commentator says the prayer upon the Prophet is accepted, so the poet placed it at beginning and end for acceptance of the whole work.
This shows the deep reverence for the Prophet in Islamic scholarship.
3
Grasp the perpetual nature of blessings
The phrase 'perpetual' refers to the favor and fruit of the blessings, not the utterances themselves, which are temporal accidents.
This resolves a potential theological confusion about how a temporal act can be perpetual.
4
Explore the meaning of 'daabuhu al-marahim'
The Prophet's habit (daab) is mercy (marahim). This means his innate disposition is mercy, extending even to disbelievers by delaying punishment.
This connects to Quran 21:107.
5
Reflect on the mercy to the worlds
The commentator ties the phrase to the Qur'anic verse, showing that the Prophet's mission is mercy for all, including disbelievers, by delaying punishment.
This highlights the comprehensive nature of prophetic mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ الدَّائِمُ عَلَى نَبِيٌّ دَابَهُ المَرَاحِمُ. وَلَمَّا كانت الصَّلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مقبولة غير مردودة .. ختم كتابَهُ بها بعد البداءة بها لتكون وسيلة لقبولِ ما بينهما؛ فقال : (ثُمَّ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ الدَّائِمُ كلُّ مِنهما، أي: الدَّائمُ فضلهما وثمرتُهما؛ لأنهما عَرضَان ينقضيان بمُجرَّد النُّطْقِ بهما) (عَلى نَبِيٌّ دَابَهُ) ، أي : عَادِتُه المُستمِرَّةُ (المَرَاحِمُ) الكاملة ، جمعُ مَرْحَمَةٍ، بمعنى الرُّحْم أو الرَّحْمَةِ، والمعنى: ثُمَّ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ على نبي موصوف بأنَّهُ لا عادة له إلا المَرَاحِمُ ، أي : شِيمَتُه وَخَلَائِقُه التي وَالشَّفَقةُ ، فرجعَ النَّظم حينئذ إلى قوله تعالى ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَكَ إِلَّا رَحْمَةً لِلْعَالَمِينَ ﴾ [الأنبياء : ۱۰۷] حتّى للكُفَّار بتأخير العذاب، فلم يُعاجَلوا بالعقوبة كسائر الأُمم المُكذِّبَةِ، النَّاسُ أحوج إليها منهم لغيرِهَا زمنَ البعثة الرَّحمةُ واللُّطْفُ.
Then the prayer and peace [be] perpetual upon a prophet whose habit is mercies. And when the prayer upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) was accepted, not rejected, he concluded his book with it after beginning with it, to be a means of acceptance of what is between them. So he said: 'Then the prayer and peace perpetual, each of them, i.e., their favor and fruit are perpetual, because they are accidents that cease upon mere utterance, upon a prophet whose habit is [continual habit] the perfect mercies, plural of 'marhamah', meaning 'ruhm' or 'rahmah'. And the meaning: Then prayer and peace upon a prophet described as having no habit except mercies, i.e., his nature and his traits which are compassion and tenderness. So the verse then goes back to His saying: 'And We sent you not but as a mercy to the worlds' (Al-Anbiya 107), even to the unbelievers by delaying punishment, so they were not hastened to punishment like other denying nations. The people are more in need of it than of other things at the time of the mission: mercy and kindness.
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the line of poetry that invokes blessings and peace upon the Prophet. The author begins by noting that the prayer upon the Prophet is accepted and not rejected, so the poet framed his work with it at the beginning and end for acceptance. Then he explains the phrase 'the prayer and peace perpetual' – each is described as perpetual in terms of its favor and fruit, since the utterance itself is transient. The word 'daabahu' means his continuous habit, and 'al-marahim' (mercies) is the plural of 'marhamah', meaning mercy. The Prophet is portrayed as one whose sole habit is mercy, which refers to his innate disposition and traits of compassion. The author then connects this to the Qur'anic verse 'We sent you not but as a mercy to the worlds', explaining that this mercy extends even to disbelievers by withholding immediate punishment. He concludes that at the time of the Prophet's mission, people were in greater need of this mercy and kindness than of anything else.

المراحم
عرض
رحمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The blessings on the Prophet are merely a verbal formality with no lasting effect.
Correction: The commentator stresses that the blessings are perpetual in their divine reward and rooted in the Prophet's essential character as mercy.

Checkpoint

B) The Prophet's continuous habit is mercies

D) The Prophet's habit changes over time

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's very nature is mercy, and blessings upon him are perpetual in their divine reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's habit was mercy, even to those who rejected him. When you face someone who has wronged you, does mercy define your response, or do you seek revenge? What one step can you take today to make mercy your constant habit?
?

?
At the time of the mission, people were most in need of mercy and kindness. What is the greatest need for mercy in your own life right now—toward yourself, your family, or your community? Are you actively seeking that mercy through the Prophet's example, or relying on your own efforts?

The Scope of Salawat: Family and Followers
Explanation of the poem's line on salawat for Prophet, his Companions, family, and followers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prayer on the Prophet extends to include his Companions, his family, and all followers of his path until the Day of Resurrection.

Core Idea
The Prophet's salawat encompasses his family and all who follow his path.

This lesson examines a line from the Jawharat al-Tawhid that expands the scope of the prayer and peace upon the Prophet. The commentator explains how the poem specifies the Prophet by name and then includes his Companions and family, and finally generalizes the blessing to every follower of his way until the end of time. Understanding this helps us appreciate the comprehensive mercy of the Prophet's mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the order: the poet begins with Muhammad, then his Companions, then his family, and finally generalizes to all followers.
The author explains that 'Muhammad' substitutes for 'the Prophet' to specify.
2
Define the key terms
Identify what 'sahb', 'itrah', 'tabi'', and 'nahj' mean. 'Itrah' refers to the Prophet's household, and 'tabi' li-nahjihi' means a follower of his path and sunnah.
3
Analyze the generalization
Notice that after specifying the Prophet's Companions and family, the poet generalizes the prayer to every follower of his path from his community. The author says this generalization is to indicate the reality, as all his states are mercy.
This shows the prayer is not limited to a specific group.
4
Apply the lesson
Consider how this understanding affects your recitation of salawat and your view of the community of believers. The prayer includes all who follow the Prophet's way, emphasizing unity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُحَمَّدٍ وَصَحْبِهِ وَعِتْرَتِهِ وَتَابِعٍ لِنَهْجِهِ مِن أُمَّتِهِ. وعيَّن المُرادَ مِن النبي بإبدال (مُحَمَّدٍ) (وَصَحْبِهِ) ، أي : والصَّلاة والسَّلام على صَحْبِه (وَ) على (عِتْرَتِه ، بالمُثناة فوق ، وهم أهل بيته . ثُمَّ عمَّمَ في الدُّعاء لأفضليته ، فقال (وَتَابع)، أي: والصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ على كُلِّ مُتَّبِعِ لِنَهْجِهِ) أي: طَريقته صلى الله عليه وسلم وَسُنَّتِه (مِنْ أُمَّتِه) أي مِن جميع إجابته من أهل طاعته إلى يوم القيامة ، وهذا القيد لبيان الواقع؛ لأنَّ جميع أحواله.
Muhammad and his Companions and his family and a follower of his path from his community. And he specified the intended meaning of 'the Prophet' by substituting 'Muhammad' and 'his Companions', i.e., prayer and peace upon his Companions and upon his family (by the dotted letter above them, i.e., his household). Then he generalized in the supplication for its excellence, so he said: 'and a follower', i.e., prayer and peace upon every follower of his path, i.e., his way and his sunnah, from his community, i.e., from all those who respond to him, among the people of his obedience until the Day of Resurrection. And this restriction is to indicate the reality, because all his states [are mercy].
Source pages p. 640

Commentary
This passage explains the next line of the poem. The author notes that the poet specified the referent of 'the Prophet' by substituting the name 'Muhammad' and then mentioning his Companions and his family ('itrah, meaning his household). After that, he generalized the prayer to include every follower of the Prophet's path (his way and sunnah) from his community. The author emphasizes that this generalization is not restrictive but rather descriptive of the reality, as all the Prophet's states are mercy. The phrase 'from his community' clarifies that these are the ones who respond to him and obey him, including all believers until the end of time.

Key Takeaway

The Prophet's Mercy Includes Disbelievers
Comment on Quranic mercy extending to disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's mercy extended to disbelievers through the delay of worldly punishment.

Core Idea
The Prophet's mercy delayed punishment for disbelievers, unlike previous nations.

This lesson explores a profound dimension of the Prophet's ﷺ mercy. The Quran declares him a mercy to the worlds, and scholars have explained how this mercy reaches even those who rejected his message. The passage shows that delaying punishment was a form of mercy that distinguished his nation from earlier ones.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the original Arabic and its literal English translation. Notice the key terms: رحمة (mercy), عذاب (punishment), and بعثة (mission).
The verse reference is from Surah Al-Anbiya.
2
Understand the extension of mercy
Focus on the phrase 'even to the disbelievers by delaying the punishment.' Reflect on why delaying punishment is considered a mercy.
Compare with earlier nations who were destroyed immediately.
3
Reflect on the context
Consider that people at the time of the Prophet's mission were more in need of mercy and kindness. How does this shape our understanding of his role?
4
Address a common misunderstanding
Some think mercy only applies to believers. This passage corrects that by showing it includes disbelievers through the delay of punishment.
This is a key theological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرجعَ النَّظم حينئذ إلى قوله تعالى ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَكَ إِلَّا رَحْمَةً لِلْعَالَمِينَ ﴾ [الأنبياء : ۱۰۷] حتّى للكُفَّار بتأخير العذاب، فلم يُعاجَلوا بالعقوبة النَّاسُ أحوج إليها منهم لغيرِهَا زمنَ البعثة الرَّحمةُ واللُّطْفُ كسائر الأُمم المُكذِّبَة.
So the composition then refers to His statement, the Most High: {And We have not sent you except as a mercy to the worlds} [Al-Anbiya: 107], even to the disbelievers by delaying the punishment, so they were not hastened to punishment. The people were more in need of it than of other things at the time of the mission. Mercy and kindness are like other nations that denied.
Source pages p. 640

Commentary
This passage comments on the Quranic verse that describes the Prophet ﷺ as a mercy to the worlds. It interprets the meaning to extend even to disbelievers, since the punishment of this world was delayed for them. They were not immediately destroyed as were previous nations. The phrase 'even to the disbelievers' shows the comprehensiveness of the Prophet's mercy. The passage also notes that people at the time of the mission were more in need of this mercy than anything else, and it parallels the 'mercy and kindness' shown to earlier nations who disbelieved.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The passage shows that mercy extends to disbelievers by delaying their punishment in this world.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's mercy encompasses disbelievers through the delay of worldly punishment, setting his nation apart from previous ones.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The disbelievers were given time to change. Are there areas in your life where you have been given respite but continue to ignore the call to repentance? What is holding you back?
?
The people at the time were in more need of mercy and kindness than anything else. Look at your own community today: are you offering mercy and kindness, or judgment and criticism? Start today by forgiving one person who has wronged you.
